### 12.26 Key Findings

#### What the Numbers Mean (and Don't Mean)

The headline — 31.5% EXECUTED, 48.9% MISSED/NEVER SAW — looks damning if read as a report card. It is not a report card. It is a map of where the skill's architecture succeeds at directing LLM behavior and where it fails. The agent produced a 2,357-line HTML page with genuine spatial inventions, 0 soul violations, correct design system compliance, and creative decisions that go beyond anything the skill explicitly prescribes. The question is not "did the agent fail?" but "what does the compliance pattern tell us about how to write better skills?"

#### Finding 1: Design system physics and binary constraints achieve near-perfect compliance.

Design Physics: 16/18 EXECUTED (89%). Anti-Patterns: 7/10 EXECUTED or CONSCIOUSLY SKIPPED with good judgment (70%). 10 Falsifiable Criteria: 7/10 EXECUTED or PARTIAL (70%). These sections share a common trait: they are concrete, testable, and binary. "border-radius: 0 always" leaves no room for interpretation and gets 100% compliance. "2+ named grid areas" is measurable and gets either compliance or a clear violation. This is the skill working as designed.

#### Finding 2: Process protocols are systematically invisible to the agent.

Primacy Rotation: 8/9 NEVER SAW. Metacognitive staleness detectors: 7/7 NEVER SAW. Wave-specific retrospective questions: NEVER SAW. Definition Journal: 1/18 expected entries. These are the skill's most elaborate procedural systems, and they were almost entirely unprocessed. But this finding requires nuance: **the agent DID self-evaluate** (5-layer metacognition at Passes 1.3, 3.3, 4.0, 5.0, 8.0), **DID run adversarial tests** (6 tests in Wave 5 with measurable RGB deltas and stacking gap fixes), and **DID track quality evolution across waves**. It just did these things in its own way rather than following the skill's prescribed format. The staleness detectors and rotation schedules read as an elaborate procedural overlay on something the agent was doing naturally through a simpler process.

#### Finding 3: The agent's unprescribed inventions are as significant as its prescribed compliance.

The skill does NOT prescribe: topology color system at 10 scales (58 instances), CRESCENDO density progression with named phases (sparse/medium/compact/heart/bedrock), a self-referential network map ("the page about topology IS a topology"), 42 cross-reference tags making document structure visible, velocity callouts (CD-001 pattern), phase transition markers (OD-006 pattern), or the 2x2 story grid. These are the agent's own creative responses to the content. A pure compliance audit misses this entirely. The agent read the Wave 0 content, formed the insight that "this document about topology IS ITSELF a topology," and then built spatial systems to express that insight. That is exactly what the skill wants — it just happened through creative engagement with content rather than through the skill's prescribed metacognitive protocols.

#### Finding 4: Pass count shortfall is real but its impact is debatable.

30 passes vs. 100-200 prescribed. Only Wave 0 met its minimum. This is the most clear-cut quantitative gap. However, the agent's passes were substantive — Pass 1.3 is a genuine 5-layer metacognitive assessment, Pass 2.1 applies research findings to measurable CSS changes, Pass 4.0 identifies and fixes 7 architectural issues, Pass 5.0 runs 6 adversarial tests with before/after measurements. These are not "code dumps." Whether 70 more passes of this quality would have yielded proportionally better output, or whether they would have hit diminishing returns, is a legitimate open question that this classification cannot answer.

#### Finding 5: Research gaps are real — R2 and R4 were never read.

R2-CREATIVE-LAYOUTS and R4-AXIS-INNOVATIONS (192 findings, 57% of corpus) were skipped. 4 of 9 case studies unread. This is a genuine coverage gap. The agent read R1, R3, R5, and SYNTHESIS, and applied findings from them (CRESCENDO from R3, zone transitions from R1, stacking avoidance from R5). Whether R2 and R4 would have produced additional spatial inventions for this specific content is a counterfactual question — the data here just confirms they were not read.

#### Finding 6: The compliance gradient (CONCRETE > ABSTRACT) is the most important architectural insight.

| Prescription Type | Execution Rate | Examples |
|---|---|---|
| Binary constraints (do/don't) | ~90% | border-radius:0, box-shadow:none, font trinity |
| Measurable thresholds | ~70% | 2+ grid areas, 940px container, >=15 RGB delta |
| Structured protocols | ~30% | 5-layer metacog, wave schedule, content readings |
| Process prescriptions | ~5-15% | Primacy rotation, staleness detectors, definition journal |

The skill is written as if all prescriptions have equal weight and equal probability of execution. They do not. Binary constraints are nearly guaranteed. Process prescriptions are nearly guaranteed to be ignored — not from defiance, but from how LLMs process instructions. **The skill should be redesigned around this reality** rather than treating all prescription types as equivalent.

#### Finding 7: CONSCIOUSLY SKIPPED reveals good judgment, not failure.

Only 5 items (2.1%) were consciously skipped. These are: corridor width variation (replaced by CRESCENDO padding — arguably better), fixed pass counts (agent self-determined — arguably the anti-pattern's intent), and mechanism sampling limits (agent deployed 10/20 mechanisms meaningfully). These are moments where the agent exercised creative judgment to deviate from the letter of a prescription while honoring its spirit. The skill should welcome this.

#### Finding 8: The 49 NEVER SAW items cluster in specific skill regions.

Primacy Rotation (8), Wave 3 detailed protocols (10), Wave 4-7 late-wave prescriptions (11), Metacognitive staleness (7), Engagement transitions (3). These are not scattered randomly — they cluster in the skill's most procedurally elaborate sections, typically appearing deep within subsections. This suggests a reading-depth problem: the agent processes the skill's high-level structure and early content reliably, but detailed procedural specifications buried in later sections fall below the attention threshold. The fix is structural (move critical prescriptions to high-salience positions) rather than emphatic (making them louder).

#### Summary: What This Classification Reveals About Skill Architecture

The build produced a good page while following roughly half the skill and ignoring the other half. This is not a paradox — it means the skill contains two kinds of content: (a) constraints and goals that effectively shape LLM output, and (b) elaborate process protocols that the LLM does not internalize. The agent's creative quality came from its genuine engagement with the content (Wave 0 immersion, topology insight, research application) combined with reliable design system compliance. It did NOT come from the staleness detectors, primacy rotation, definition journal, or exhaustion checks. A v2 skill should lean heavily into what works (binary constraints, measurable criteria, content-engagement triggers) and either convert process protocols into concrete checkpoints or accept that they serve as aspirational documentation rather than executable instructions.

---

## 22. Research Digestion Depth Analysis {#research-digestion-depth}
*Agent: digestion-depth-auditor | Task #26 | 2026-03-03*

### Summary Verdict

**Research digestion reached Phase 1 (STRUCTURAL) for all files, with DD-006 achieving Phase 1.3 (traces of TRANSLATION). No file reached Phase 2 (INTEGRATION) or beyond.** The skill's 4-phase model predicts qualitatively different engagement at pass 3 vs pass 7 vs pass 10. This build operated at the pass-3 level for every file.

**However, Phase 1 produced genuinely good work.** The ideas extracted at shallow depth were well-chosen and effectively applied:

- **CRESCENDO pattern** (from R3): Applied as a 56px->52px->44px->80/64px->64px padding progression that genuinely tracks the content's philosophical-to-technical velocity arc. This is not mechanical -- it required understanding the content's structure.
- **Topology color system** (from DD-006 + independent insight): 4 colors persisting across 10 scales, 58 instances. A genuine spatial invention that emerged from combining DD-006's fractal persistence principle with the builder's own "page about topology IS a topology" insight. This is creative translation, not copying.
- **Velocity callouts** (from CD-001): 8 interleaving breaks between heavy blocks. Mechanical in execution (uniform styling) but correct in placement -- the builder understood WHERE velocity interleaving was needed.
- **Phase transition markers** (from OD-006): Applied at the two most important structural boundaries in the content.

The honest assessment: the builder extracted ONE good idea from each file and applied it competently. The skill's model predicts that passes 7-10 would unlock compound insights (multi-dimensional density, fractal density vs fractal color, component differentiation by velocity). These compound insights are absent. Whether the remaining ~70% of prescribed engagement would have transformed the page or produced diminishing returns is an open question -- the hypothetical trace in Section 22.4 explores this honestly.

**The key distinction is between "what the skill prescribes" and "what matters for quality."** Some of the missing elements (24 metacognitive questions, primacy rotation schedules, definition journal entries) are process scaffolding that may or may not translate to perceptible output quality. Other missing elements (multi-dimensional density, fractal density at all scales, compound combination) are substantive and would have changed the page. This analysis attempts to distinguish between the two.

---

### 22.1 The 4-Phase Digestion Model (Skill Specification)

The skill defines a clear progression for Wave 2 (research R1-R5):

| Phase | Passes | Dominant Activity | CSS Lines/Pass | Agent's Relationship to Research | Signal Question |
|-------|--------|------------------|----------------|----------------------------------|-----------------|
| **STRUCTURAL** | 1-3 | BUILDING | 100-200 | "What does this research say I should ADD?" | Research as instruction |
| **INTEGRATION** | 4-6 | LOOKING | 50-100 | "How does this research change how I SEE relationships?" | Research as diagnostic lens |
| **DEPTH** | 7-9 | REFINING | 10-40 | "Has this research changed my understanding of the CONTENT itself?" | Research as content deepening |
| **MASTERY** | 10+ | EVALUATING | <10 | "Have I internalized this so deeply I no longer cite findings but THINK in its vocabulary?" | Research as internalized taste |

For Wave 3 (case studies), a parallel progression:

| Phase | Agent's Relationship to Case Study |
|-------|-----------------------------------|
| **EXTRACTION** | Study the PROCESS (Section 4 collapse moment), not the output |
| **TRANSLATION** | Adapt to THIS content -- does each borrowed component fail the swap test? |
| **CONTENT-DEEPENING** | Case study teaches about MY content -- features I hadn't seen before |
| **COMPOUND VISION** | DD + OD effects interact on the same elements |
| **INTERNALIZATION** | Thinking the way those builders thought -- reading own page as case study |

---

### 22.2 Per-File Digestion Analysis

#### File: R1-DOCUMENTATION-PATTERNS.md (28 findings)

**Digestion phase reached: STRUCTURAL (Phase 1 only)**

**Evidence:**
- Read once in Pass 2.0 as part of a batch read with 4 other files
- 3 of 28 findings extracted: density rhythm principle (R1-001), viewport principle (R1-003), horizontal comparison break (R1-008)
- Extraction rate: 10.7% of findings
- Never re-read. No second primacy turn.

**Checklist vs Lens test:**
- CHECKLIST. The notebook documents: "R1-008: horizontal layout ONLY for comparison (Production stories ARE comparison)." This is direct extraction-to-deployment. The finding is read, matched to a page element, and applied. The file was never used to RE-SEE existing page decisions.
- A LENS engagement would ask: "R1's density rhythm principle (HIGH/LOW/MEDIUM) -- have I checked whether my existing zone structure follows this oscillation? Are there 3 consecutive HIGH-density sections?" This question never appears.

**What COULD have been extracted but was not (partial list):**
- R1-002 (38% retention rule): whitespace improving retention -- could have quantified the spacing strategy
- R1-003 (viewport principle, partially used): "one major concept per viewport height" -- never applied as a constraint check across the page's 13 sections
- R1-004 through R1-006 (axis transitions): three-column doctrine, responsive collapse hierarchy -- entirely absent from the page design, which uses only single-column flow
- R1-007 through R1-012 (component arrangements): callout positioning doctrine, callout scarcity principle, code-adjacent patterns, progressive disclosure architecture -- never extracted despite the page having 27 code blocks, 8 velocity callouts, and 17 details elements that could have been evaluated against these patterns
- R1-013 through R1-028 (typography hierarchy, navigation patterns, progressive disclosure): entirely unread findings that address typography rhythm and navigation -- both active concerns in this build

**Pass 3 vs pass 7 vs pass 10 markers:**
- At pass 3 (STRUCTURAL): "R1 says add density rhythm. I added CRESCENDO padding." -- This is where the builder stopped.
- At pass 7 (DEPTH): The builder would ask: "R1's viewport principle says one concept per viewport. My Foundational Patterns section is 3 cards spanning 2+ viewports. Is that an R1 violation, or does the content's structure justify it? What specific content feature makes 3-card-per-viewport correct HERE?" -- Never asked.
- At pass 10 (MASTERY): The builder would no longer cite "R1 says" but would automatically evaluate density rhythm at every section, naturally asking "does this viewport serve one concept?" without referencing R1. -- Never reached.

#### File: R3-DENSITY-DIMENSIONS.md (51 findings)

**Digestion phase reached: STRUCTURAL (Phase 1 only)**

**Evidence:**
- Read once in Pass 2.0 (batch read)
- Key extraction: CRESCENDO pattern, "6 density dimensions" mentioned but not enumerated or applied
- Applied: padding progression (64->52->44 px). This maps to R3's CRESCENDO concept.
- Extraction rate: ~4-6% of findings (2-3 of 51)
- Never re-read.

**Checklist vs Lens test:**
- CHECKLIST. "R3 says CRESCENDO, I applied CRESCENDO padding." The 6-dimension density model (temporal, depth, semantic, cognitive, interaction, spatial) was noted in the notebook but never operationalized. The page's density work is exclusively SPATIAL (padding values). No temporal density (scroll velocity mapping), no depth density (progressive disclosure layers with distinct density), no semantic density (meaning-per-area analysis), no cognitive density (mental processing load mapping), no interaction density (interactive element distribution).
- A LENS engagement would ask: "R3 identifies 6 density dimensions. My page currently only manipulates spatial density (padding). What does TEMPORAL density look like for multi-agent patterns content? Where does the content accelerate?" The velocity mapping done in Wave 0 (Pass 0.6) was a proto-version of temporal density, but R3's full model was never overlaid on it.

**What COULD have been extracted but was not (from R3's 51 findings):**
- R3's depth density model (geological: surface/sediment/bedrock layers): the page HAS progressive disclosure (17 details elements) but never mapped these to R3's depth-density gradient
- R3's semantic density insight: "A single word can be semantically dense ('Kubernetes') or sparse ('the')" -- the page's code blocks contain semantically dense patterns (Panopticon, Ralph, Orchestra) that could have been given different visual treatment based on semantic density
- R3's cognitive density: "Mental processing required per viewport" -- never mapped across the page's 13 sections
- R3's interaction density: "Interactive elements per viewport" -- never evaluated (17 details elements are the only interactive elements, unevenly distributed)
- R3's fractal self-similarity (R3-023): Mentioned indirectly via DD-006 case study absorption, but the research-level understanding of WHY fractal density works (same rhythm at every zoom level) was never connected to the page's topology color system (which IS fractal across 10 scales but was never identified as density-fractal)
- R3's PULSE, BOOKENDS, and WAVE patterns: Only CRESCENDO was extracted. The content's structure (Vision -> Mechanics -> Architecture -> Reference) could have been mapped to BOOKENDS (dense opening philosophy + dense closing reference, sparse middle mechanics)

**Dimension-specific metacognitive questions (from skill) -- NEVER ASKED:**
- "Am I treating density as a SINGLE dimension (spatial), or have I absorbed R3's 6-dimension density model?" -- **ANSWER: single dimension (spatial only). The builder never absorbed the multi-dimensional model.**
- "Have I identified the content's VELOCITY MAP and does my page's density rhythm track it?" -- **PARTIALLY: Wave 0 Pass 0.6 mapped velocity, but R3's model was never overlaid to validate or deepen it.**
- "Does the page have decompression zones? Or is density applied uniformly?" -- **PARTIALLY: zone backgrounds alternate, but no explicit decompression zones were designed as R3 prescribes.**

Should the Panopticon setup commands (FAST) look different from the 50-line architecture config (HEAVY)?" -- Never asked.

- R5's sequence principles: ordering rules for component types -- never consulted for the page's section ordering
- R5's nesting rules: containment patterns -- 17 details elements contain various component types, but nesting rules were never consulted

---

#### File: DD-006-fractal.md (378 lines)

**Digestion phase reached: EXTRACTION (Phase 1) with traces of TRANSLATION (Phase 2)**

**This was the most deeply engaged file of all research files.** Referenced 3 times (Pass 3.0, Pass 3.1, Pass 4.3). The fractal self-similarity principle became the topology color system's conceptual backbone: 4 colors persisting across 10 scales, 58 instances.

**Evidence of EXTRACTION (Phase 1):**
- Pass 3.0: Read and extracted "Fractal self-similarity across 4 structural scales. 6 reusable mechanisms."
- Pass 3.1: Applied "DD-006 fractal scale persistence" -- topology colors added to 6 sections at section-level borders
- The 6 mechanisms listed (dense/sparse alternation, spacing compression, border-weight gradient, zone background differentiation, typographic scale jumping, 2-zone component DNA) were partially deployed

**Evidence of partial TRANSLATION (Phase 2) -- the strongest research engagement in the build:**
- Pass 4.3: "Fractal Scale Persistence" verification -- topology colors counted across 10 distinct scales, 58 instances. This goes beyond raw extraction into systematic application.
- The topology color system IS a genuine translation of fractal density -- it takes DD-006's principle (same pattern at all scales) and applies it to THIS content's 4-topology classification system. This is not a copy -- it is a spatial invention. The builder saw that the content's 4-topology taxonomy (Hub, Peer, Factory, Kanban) could be encoded as a persistent color system visible at every structural level. DD-006 provided the principle; the builder provided the content-specific application.
- **This is the build's strongest example of research producing creative output.** Even at Phase 1.3, the DD-006 engagement produced something the page would be noticeably worse without.

**Where deeper engagement would have added value (TRANSLATION incomplete):**
- The swap test was never applied. DD-006's fractal rhythm includes dense/sparse alternation at EVERY scale (page, section, component, character). The builder applied fractal to COLOR persistence but not to DENSITY rhythm at multiple scales. The page does not have fractal density -- it has fractal color. The density is CRESCENDO (linear gradient), not fractal (self-similar at every scale).
- DD-006's "2-zone component DNA" mechanism was noted but the builder never asked: "Do my components have 2-zone DNA? Do my pattern cards have a sparse label zone and a dense content zone?" Some do (pattern cards have a header row + content grid), but this was not derived from DD-006 -- it was an independent structural choice.
- DD-006's "collapse moment" (Section 4) -- "Realizing fractal doesn't just mean nested -- it means THE SAME RHYTHM VISIBLE AT EVERY ZOOM LEVEL" -- was not internalized. The builder's fractal is nested (colors at many scales) but not rhythmic (same dense/sparse alternation at every scale).

**CONTENT-DEEPENING (Phase 3) never reached:**
- The skill predicts at Phase 3: "the case study teaches about MY content -- features I hadn't seen before." DD-006 could have taught the builder that the multi-agent patterns content has a FRACTAL STRUCTURE -- the Panopticon pattern (domain-isolated parallelism) contains sub-patterns (file isolation, git worktrees, Docker containers) that themselves contain sub-sub-patterns (lock files, branch strategies, volume mounts). This self-similar structure was identified in Wave 0 Pass 0.7 ("Not linear. A NETWORK.") but was never reconnected to DD-006's fractal model to deepen it.
- The builder never asked: "Does DD-006 teach me something about my content that I didn't know before reading it?" If asked, the answer would be: "Yes -- the content's pattern taxonomy is ITSELF fractal. Architecture Patterns (Hub, Peer, Factory, Kanban) each contain sub-patterns (Panopticon=Hub+isolation, Ralph=Kanban+iteration, Orchestra=Factory+specialization). The page could encode this at 3 structural scales: topology level, pattern level, implementation level."

**Dimension-specific metacognitive questions (from skill) -- NEVER ASKED:**
- "Am I seeing density at 3+ scales (section, component, character)? Or only at one?" -- **Color at 10 scales, density at 1 scale (section padding only)**
- "Does the dense/sparse alternation track the content's VELOCITY?" -- **Partially (CRESCENDO tracks velocity gradient) but not fractally (same rhythm at every scale)**
- "Does the border-weight gradient encode content hierarchy, or is it decorative?" -- **Mixed: topology borders are semantic (color = topology type), border weight is uniform (3px for all section borders). No weight gradient encoding hierarchy.**

#### File: CD-001-reasoning-inside-code.md (416 lines)

**Digestion phase reached: EXTRACTION (Phase 1 only)**

**Evidence:**
- Read once in Pass 3.0 (batch read)
- Single extraction: velocity interleaving -- "never stack same-velocity components"
- Applied: 8 velocity callouts inserted between heavy blocks across the page

**Checklist vs Lens test:**
- CHECKLIST. The most transparent checklist pattern in the entire build. "CD-001 says velocity interleaving -> I added velocity callouts between heavy blocks." The callouts themselves are uniform (all use the same 3px red border, white background, italic text). CD-001's deeper insight -- that component VELOCITY matters more than component TYPE -- was noted but never applied beyond the mechanical insertion of callout breaks.
- A LENS engagement would ask: "CD-001's velocity framework identifies HEAVY, MEDIUM, and FAST components. What are MY page's component velocity signatures? My 27 code blocks -- are they all HEAVY, or do some (short bash one-liners) qualify as FAST? If some code blocks are FAST, do they need the same interleaving treatment as HEAVY code blocks?" -- Never asked.

**What COULD have been extracted but was not:**
- CD-001's F-Pattern to Bento transition via BRIDGE: The page has no axis transitions. CD-001 shows how to transition FROM vertical scanning (F-pattern) TO grid layout (Bento) using a BRIDGE element. The page's Architecture Patterns section (2x2 topology grid) IS a Bento moment, but no BRIDGE transition grammar was applied at its entry.
- CD-001's CRESCENDO density in narrative arc (sparse intro -> dense peak -> sparse resolution): The builder applied CRESCENDO independently from R3, but CD-001's version ties density to NARRATIVE ARC (Freytag structure). The content HAS a narrative arc (Vision -> Mechanics -> Architecture heart -> Reference). CD-001 could have been used as a lens to verify that the density gradient TRACKS this arc.
- CD-001's "collapse moment" (heavy clustering at climax via Bento): The page's Architecture Patterns section is the conceptual "climax" and uses a 2x2 grid -- this IS a Bento cluster at the climax. But this was an independent design choice, not derived from CD-001. The connection was never made in the notebook.

**TRANSLATION (Phase 2) never reached:**
- The swap test was never applied to the velocity callouts. All 8 callouts are generic italic phrases ("Three philosophies, one ecosystem," "The conductor/instrument split is fundamental"). These PASS the swap test -- they could be transplanted to ANY technical content page. CD-001's TRANSLATION phase would require callouts that are specific to THIS content and fail the swap test.
